          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER
          can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
          missed by single-gene strategies.

          Genes work together in specific contexts to perform their functions,
          and understanding how these genes influence complex traits requires a
          mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across different
          conditions. This insight is crucial for developing new therapies, and
          transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models predict that gene-gene interactions play a critical role in
          disease origin and progression. To address this challenge, we
          introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across relevant
          cell types. We find that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and reveals mechanisms of
          action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
          regulation, we identify functionally important players that lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER
          can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
          missed by single-gene strategies.

      response:
        output: >-
          Genes coordinate their actions in specific contexts to perform their
          functions, but determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. While transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a
          crucial role in disease origin and progression. To address this gap,
          we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across relevant
          cell types. We find that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER
          accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and inferences mechanisms
          of action. Furthermore, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes,
          PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential
          targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our approach provides a
          powerful tool for identifying therapeutic targets and drug repurposing
          opportunities, advancing our understanding of the complex interplay
          between genetic variations and disease mechanisms.

      response:
        output: >-
          In the field of complex trait research, understanding how genes
          interact with each other in specific contexts is crucial for
          developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a
          critical role in disease origin and progression. Here, we introduce
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations
          and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
          representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on
          modules of genes with similar expression patterns across relevant cell
          types. We find that diseases are significantly associated with gene
          modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately
          predicts known drug-disease pairs and inferts mechanisms of action.
          Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we
          find that functionally important players lack associations but are
          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. By
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER contextualizes
          genetic associations and reveals potential targets missed by
          single-gene strategies. Our approach provides a powerful tool for
          understanding the complex interplay between genes in disease
          mechanisms, and has important implications for the development of new
          therapies.

      response:
        output: >-
          In this study, we aim to uncover the complex relationships between
          genes, traits, and drugs by integrating multiple types of genomic
          data. We employ a novel computational approach called PhenoPLIER,
          which maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation. This representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across different
          conditions, allowing us to identify disease-associated gene modules
          and prioritize potential drug targets. By incorporating co-expression
          information, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and
          reveal hidden relationships between genes, traits, and drugs. We
          demonstrate the power of PhenoPLIER by applying it to a CRISPR screen
          for lipid regulation, where we identify functionally important players
          that lack direct associations with disease but are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules. Our findings highlight the importance of
          considering gene co-expression patterns when interpreting genetic
          associations and identifying potential drug targets.

          roles, yet determining how these genes influence complex traits

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript. Revise the following abstract of
          this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure and fits in
          a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER
          can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
          missed by single-gene strategies.

        display: >-

      response:
        output: >-
          In the field of complex trait research, understanding how genes
          interact with each other to influence disease mechanisms is crucial
          for developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association
          studies have helped identify individual gene variants associated with
          disease, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a
          critical role in disease origin and progression. Here, we introduce
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene expression
          data and pharmacological perturbation information to identify gene
          modules associated with complex traits. By mapping these modules to
          relevant cell types, we find that diseases are significantly
          associated with genes expressed in these cell types, and our approach
          accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and reveals mechanisms of
          action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
          regulation, we identify functionally important players that lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER
          contextualizes genetic associations and reveals potential targets
          missed by single-gene strategies, advancing our understanding of
          complex disease mechanisms.

          Genes collaborate in specific contexts to execute their functions.
          Uncovering how these genes contribute to complex traits requires a

          Revised abstract:


          Title: Projecting Genetic Associations through Gene Expression
          Patterns Highlights Disease Etiology and Drug Mechanisms


          Keywords: genetic studies, functional genomics, gene co-expression,
          therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering of complex traits.


          Abstract:


          Genes interact in concert to perform their functions, and
          understanding how these interactions contribute to complex diseases is
          crucial for developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide
          association studies have identified the role of individual genes in
          disease mechanisms, recent models suggest that gene-gene interactions
          play a significant role in disease etiology and progression. To
          address this challenge, we developed PhenoPLIER, a computational
          approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a unified latent representation for joint
          analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
          similar expression patterns across the same conditions. Our findings
          show that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
          expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts
          known drug-disease pairs and reveals mechanisms of action.
          Additionally, through a CRISPR screen targeting lipid regulation, we
          identify functionally important players that lack genetic associations
          but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. By
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential therapeutic
          targets missed by single-gene strategies.

          * "Uncovering how these genes contribute to complex traits requires a
          mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across various
          conditions, which is crucial for developing novel therapies." becomes
          "Understanding how these interactions contribute to complex diseases
          is crucial for developing new therapies."

          role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms." becomes

          progression."

          analysis." becomes "To address this challenge, we developed
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait

          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions."

          * "Our findings show that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER

          action." becomes "Our findings show that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and

      response:
        output: >-
          Projecting genetic associations through gene expression patterns
          highlights disease etiology and drug mechanisms. Despite advances in
          genetic studies, functional genomics, and gene co-expression analysis,
          there remains a significant gap in understanding how gene variants
          contribute to complex traits and drug responses. Existing methods have
          primarily focused on individual genes or small sets of genes,
          neglecting the importance of gene modules and their expression
          patterns across different conditions. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
          computational approach that integrates transcriptome-wide association
          studies, pharmacological perturbation data, and gene co-expression
          analysis to map gene-trait associations in a joint manner. By
          leveraging the power of modules of genes with similar expression
          patterns, PhenoPLIER identifies disease-associated gene modules that
          are enriched for functionally important genes. We demonstrate the
          accuracy of PhenoPLIER by predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Additionally, we use a CRISPR screen
          to analyze lipid regulation and show that functionally important
          players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
          modules by PhenoPLIER. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes,
          PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential
          targets missed by single-gene strategies, advancing our understanding
          of disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug

          abstract of this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure
          and fits in a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER
          can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
          missed by single-gene strategies.

        output: >-
          Projecting genetic associations through gene expression patterns
          highlights disease etiology and drug mechanisms. Despite the wealth of
          genetic studies on complex traits, a mechanistic understanding of how
          genes interact to influence these conditions remains elusive. Current
          approaches often focus on individual genes or small sets of genes,
          neglecting the context-dependent interactions between genes that are
          critical for disease origin and progression. Here, we introduce
          PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that integrates gene
          expression patterns and pharmacological perturbation data to identify
          gene modules associated with complex traits. By mapping these modules
          onto known drug-disease associations, PhenoPLIER reveals potential
          therapeutic targets missed by single-gene strategies. Using a CRISPR
          screen to analyze lipid regulation, we demonstrate the utility of
          PhenoPLIER in identifying functionally important players lacking
          genetic associations but prioritized in trait-associated modules. Our
          findings highlight the importance of considering gene expression
          patterns in genetic association studies and provide insights into the
          mechanisms underlying complex traits.

          Revised abstract:


          Title: Projecting Genetic Associations through Gene Expression
          Patterns Highlights Disease Etiology and Drug Mechanisms


          Keywords: genetic studies, functional genomics, gene co-expression,
          therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering of complex traits


          Abstract:


          Genes collaborate in specific contexts to execute their functions.
          Uncovering how these genes contribute to complex traits requires a
          mechanistic understanding of expression regulation under different
          conditions. This insight is crucial for developing novel therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped identify the role
          of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models predict that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in
          disease onset and progression. To address this challenge, we developed
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified
          latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based
          on modules of co-expressed genes across the same conditions. We find
          that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
          in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known
          drug-disease pairs and reveals mechanisms of action. In addition, by
          leveraging a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we identify
          functionally important players that lack genetic associations but are
          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. By
          incorporating co-expression patterns, PhenoPLIER can contextualize
          genetic associations and uncover potential targets missed by
          single-gene strategies. Our findings highlight the power of
          integrating gene expression patterns with genetic associations to
          project disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          In the field of genetic studies, there is a significant gap in our
          understanding of how genes interact with each other to influence
          complex traits. While transcriptome-wide association studies have
          helped identify individual genes associated with disease mechanisms,

          groups of co-expressed genes to contextualize genetic associations and
          identify functional players in disease etiology. Our findings provide
          a comprehensive understanding of how gene expression patterns
          contribute to complex traits and pave the way for new therapeutic
          strategies.

        output: >-
          Here we present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that
          integrates gene expression data with genetic associations and drug
          perturbation information to identify key genes associated with complex
          diseases. By mapping these genes into functional modules based on
          co-expression patterns, we show that diseases are significantly
          enriched in modules expressed in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER
          accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and reveals potential
          mechanisms of action by prioritizing functionally important players in
          trait-associated modules. In a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation, we
          find that co-expressed genes are enriched in trait-associated modules,
          highlighting the importance of contextualizing genetic associations
          using gene expression data. Our approach demonstrates that
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes can reveal potential
          targets missed by single-gene strategies and provide a mechanistic
          understanding of expression regulation across different conditions. By
          integrating multiple types of data, PhenoPLIER provides a
          comprehensive framework for identifying key genes in complex disease
          etiology and drug mechanism, supporting the development of new
          therapies.

          In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that
          integrates gene expression data with genetic associations and drug
          perturbation information to identify key genes associated with complex
          diseases. By mapping these genes into functional modules based on
          co-expression patterns, we show that diseases are significantly
          enriched in modules expressed in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER
          accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and reveals potential
          mechanisms of action by prioritizing functionally important players in
          trait-associated modules. In a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation, we
          find that co-expressed genes are enriched in trait-associated modules,
          highlighting the importance of contextualizing genetic associations
          using gene expression data. Our approach demonstrates that
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes can reveal potential
          targets missed by single-gene strategies and provide a mechanistic
          understanding of expression regulation across different conditions. By
          integrating multiple types of data, PhenoPLIER provides a
          comprehensive framework for identifying key genes in complex disease
          etiology and drug mechanism, supporting the development of new
          therapies.

          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is

          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the

          Here we present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational framework for
          integrating genetic association studies with functional genomics data
          to identify key genes and pathways involved in complex diseases. By
          analyzing gene expression patterns across different conditions,
          PhenoPLIER creates a shared latent space for genetic associations and
          drug mechanisms, allowing for the identification of disease-specific
          gene modules that are associated with therapeutic targets. Using a
          CRISPR screen to investigate lipid regulation, we demonstrate that
          PhenoPLIER can prioritize functionally important genes that lack
          direct genetic associations but are enriched in trait-associated gene
          modules. By incorporating co-expression patterns, PhenoPLIER provides
          a more comprehensive understanding of the genetic basis of complex
          traits, revealing potential therapeutic targets missed by single-gene
          approaches. The regulation of gene expression is context-dependent and
          involves interactions between multiple genes, making it essential to
          consider these relationships when investigating disease mechanisms.
          Recent studies have shown that incorporating functional genomics data
          into genetic association analyses can improve the accuracy of disease
          prediction and reveal novel therapeutic targets. PhenoPLIER offers a
          powerful tool for integrating these different types of data to better
          understand the complex interplay between genetic and environmental
          factors in human health and disease.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript. Revise the following abstract of
          this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure and fits in
          a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
          approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
          analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
          similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe
          that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
          in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting
          known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action.
          Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we
          find that functionally important players lack associations but are
          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. By
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed
          by single-gene strategies. Genes act in concert with each other in
          specific contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these
          genes influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.

          In this manuscript, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational
          approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
          analysis. By leveraging the expression patterns of genes across
          different conditions, we identify disease associations with gene
          modules expressed in relevant cell types, demonstrating high accuracy
          in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
          action. Furthermore, through a CRISPR screen focused on lipid

          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. The integration of

          that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
          progression. By filling this gap in our understanding, PhenoPLIER
          offers a powerful tool for uncovering the complex interplay between
          genetic and environmental factors in disease etiology.

          in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting
          known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action.
          Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we
          find that functionally important players lack associations but are
          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. By
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed
          by single-gene strategies. Genes act in concert with each other in
          specific contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these

          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown

          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.

          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. We observe that diseases are
          significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell
          types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease
          pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR
          screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally
          important players lack associations but are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER,
          a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation
          for a joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes
          with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. By
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed
          by single-gene strategies.
      response:
        output: >-
          In this study, we investigate the interplay between genetic variations
          and gene expression patterns in complex diseases. By integrating
          genome-wide association studies (GWAS) with transcriptome-wide
          association studies (TWAS), we identify gene modules associated with
          disease risk factors and drug mechanisms. Our approach leverages the
          power of functional genomics to capture the underlying biology, rather
          than relying solely on single-gene associations. We demonstrate the
          accuracy of our method by predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          identifying novel therapeutic targets. Furthermore, we use a CRISPR
          screen to investigate lipid regulation and show that functionally
          important players are prioritized in trait-associated modules. To
          contextualize genetic associations, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
          computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation.
          This representation is based on modules of co-expressed genes,
          allowing us to identify potential targets missed by single-gene
          strategies. Our findings highlight the importance of considering the
          complex interplay between genetic variations and gene expression
          patterns in disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          novel therapeutic targets.

          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. We
          observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
          expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
          predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
          action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
          regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. This
          representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression
          patterns across the same conditions. By incorporating groups of
          co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations
          and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies.

          functions, and understanding how these genes contribute to complex

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure
          and fits in a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes,
          PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential
          targets missed by single-gene strategies. We observe that diseases are
          significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell
          types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease
          pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR
          screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally
          important players lack associations but are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

        output: >-
          In the field of genetic studies, identifying the underlying mechanisms
          of complex traits remains a significant challenge. While
          transcriptome-wide association studies have provided valuable insights
          into the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms,
          modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role
          in disease origin and progression. To address this gap, we introduce
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene expression
          patterns and pharmacological perturbation data to identify gene-trait
          associations. By grouping co-expressed genes into modules, PhenoPLIER
          contextualizes genetic associations and reveals potential targets
          missed by single-gene strategies. We demonstrate the accuracy of
          PhenoPLIER in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. Our approach fills a significant gap in the current
          literature, providing a mechanistic understanding of complex traits
          and identifying potential therapeutic targets.

          In the field of complex trait research, understanding how genes
          interact with each other in specific contexts is crucial for
          developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant

          etiology.

          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across

          In the field of genetic studies, there is a significant gap in
          understanding how genes interact with each other to contribute to
          complex traits. While transcriptome-wide association studies have
          helped identify individual genes associated with disease mechanisms,
          modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role
          in disease origin and progression. To address this gap, we introduce
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene expression
          patterns and pharmacological perturbation data to identify groups of
          co-expressed genes (modules) associated with specific traits. By

          demonstrate the accuracy of PhenoPLIER by predicting known
          drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Additionally,
          using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that
          functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized
          in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our approach fills a
          critical gap in the current literature by providing a comprehensive
          framework for understanding the complex interplay between genes and
          their role in disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          lack of a comprehensive approach to integrate gene-gene interactions

              have helped uncover the role of individual genes in

              play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we

              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. By
              incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
              contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies.

              portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader
              field forward (e.g. "broader significance").

              In this study, we aim to uncover the complex relationships between
              genes, traits, and drugs by integrating multiple types of genomic
              data. We employ a novel computational approach called PhenoPLIER,
              which maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation. This
              representation is based on modules of genes with similar
              expression patterns across different conditions, allowing us to
              identify disease-associated gene modules and prioritize potential
              drug targets. By incorporating co-expression information,
              PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
              hidden relationships between genes, traits, and drugs. We
              demonstrate the power of PhenoPLIER by applying it to a CRISPR
              screen for lipid regulation, where we identify functionally
              important players that lack direct associations with disease but
              are prioritized in trait-associated modules. Our findings
              highlight the importance of considering gene co-expression
              patterns when interpreting genetic associations and identifying
              potential drug targets.

              mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across various
              conditions, which is crucial for developing novel therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped identify the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              recent models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a
              significant role in disease etiology and progression. To address
              this challenge, we developed PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
              that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a unified latent representation for joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. Our
              findings show that diseases are significantly associated with gene
              modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER
              accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and reveals
              mechanisms of action. Additionally, through a CRISPR screen
              targeting lipid regulation, we identify functionally important
              players that lack genetic associations but are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. By incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential therapeutic targets missed by
              single-gene strategies.


              Revised abstract:


              Title: Projecting Genetic Associations through Gene Expression
              Patterns Highlights Disease Etiology and Drug Mechanisms


              Keywords: genetic studies, functional genomics, gene
              co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering
              of complex traits.


              Abstract:


              Genes interact in concert to perform their functions, and
              understanding how these interactions contribute to complex
              diseases is crucial for developing new therapies. While
              transcriptome-wide association studies have identified the role of
              individual genes in disease mechanisms, recent models suggest that
              gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease etiology
              and progression. To address this challenge, we developed
              PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified
              latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is
              based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
              the same conditions. Our findings show that diseases are
              significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease
              pairs and reveals mechanisms of action. Additionally, through a
              CRISPR screen targeting lipid regulation, we identify functionally
              important players that lack genetic associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. By
              incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
              contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential
              therapeutic targets missed by single-gene strategies.

              Projecting genetic associations through gene expression patterns
              highlights disease etiology and drug mechanisms. Despite advances
              in genetic studies, functional genomics, and gene co-expression
              analysis, there remains a significant gap in understanding how
              gene variants contribute to complex traits and drug responses.
              Existing methods have primarily focused on individual genes or
              small sets of genes, neglecting the importance of gene modules and
              their expression patterns across different conditions. Here, we
              introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates
              transcriptome-wide association studies, pharmacological
              perturbation data, and gene co-expression analysis to map
              gene-trait associations in a joint manner. By leveraging the power
              of modules of genes with similar expression patterns, PhenoPLIER
              identifies disease-associated gene modules that are enriched for
              functionally important genes. We demonstrate the accuracy of
              PhenoPLIER by predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action. Additionally, we use a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation and show that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. By incorporating groups of co-expressed
              genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and
              reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies,
              advancing our understanding of disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms.

              Genes collaborate in specific contexts to execute their functions.
              Uncovering how these genes contribute to complex traits requires a

              modules by PhenoPLIER. By incorporating co-expression patterns,
              PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and uncover
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies.

              Title: Projecting Genetic Associations through Gene Expression
              Patterns Highlights Disease Etiology and Drug Mechanisms


              Keywords: genetic studies, functional genomics, gene
              co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering

              Abstract:


              Genes collaborate in specific contexts to execute their functions.
              Uncovering how these genes contribute to complex traits requires a
              mechanistic understanding of expression regulation under different
              conditions. This insight is crucial for developing novel
              therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped
              identify the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
              mechanisms. However, modern models predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a pivotal role in disease onset and progression.
              To address this challenge, we developed PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent
              representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on
              modules of co-expressed genes across the same conditions. We find
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately
              predicts known drug-disease pairs and reveals mechanisms of
              action. In addition, by leveraging a CRISPR screen to analyze
              lipid regulation, we identify functionally important players that
              lack genetic associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. By incorporating co-expression patterns,
              PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and uncover
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our findings
              highlight the power of integrating gene expression patterns with
              genetic associations to project disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms.

              integrates gene expression data with genetic associations and drug
              perturbation information to identify key genes associated with

              new therapies.

              pharmacological perturbation data to identify functionally
              important modules of co-expressed genes associated with complex
              traits. By contextualizing genetic associations through gene
              expression patterns, PhenoPLIER can reveal potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies and provide insights into drug
              mechanisms. Our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease
              pairs and identifies novel therapeutic targets for complex traits,
              advancing the field of functional genomics and personalized
              medicine.

              on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the
              same conditions. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes,

              mechanisms, and highlight the potential of PhenoPLIER as a
              powerful tool for identifying new therapeutic targets.


              In the broader field of complex trait genetics, there is a
              significant gap in our understanding of how genes interact with
              each other to influence disease mechanisms. While
              transcriptome-wide association studies (TWAS) have helped uncover
              the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms,
              modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial
              role in disease origin and progression. Our research aims to fill
              this gap by developing a novel computational approach, PhenoPLIER,
              which integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data to identify functionally important players in
              disease mechanisms. By leveraging the power of TWAS and CRISPR
              screens, we find that diseases are significantly associated with
              gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
              accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action.


              The results of our study have significant implications for the
              field of complex trait genetics. By demonstrating the importance
              of considering gene-gene interactions in understanding disease
              mechanisms, we highlight the potential of PhenoPLIER as a powerful
              tool for identifying new therapeutic targets. Our approach can be
              used to identify gene modules associated with specific diseases,
              and to prioritize these modules based on their functional
              importance. This has the potential to revolutionize our
              understanding of complex disease mechanisms and lead to the
              development of new and effective therapies.

              predicting the crucial role of gene-gene interactions. Here, we
              introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for joint analysis. By
              incorporating co-expressed genes into modules, PhenoPLIER
              contextualizes genetic associations and identifies potential
              targets missed by single-gene strategies. We demonstrate the
              accuracy of PhenoPLIER in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
              inferring mechanisms of action, as well as its ability to identify
              functionally important players lacking associations but
              prioritized in trait-associated modules. This work advances the
              field by providing a powerful tool for understanding the complex
              interplay between genes in disease origins and progression.

              Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
              contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
              influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
              expression regulation across different conditions. It has been
              shown that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. By
              incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
              contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies. We observe that diseases are
              significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action.
              Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we
              find that functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

              In the field of genetic studies, there is a significant gap in
              understanding how genes interact with each other to contribute to
              complex traits. While transcriptome-wide association studies have

              integrates gene expression patterns and pharmacological

              (modules) associated with specific traits. By contextualizing

              screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally
              important players lack associations but are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our approach fills a
              critical gap in the current literature by providing a
              comprehensive framework for understanding the complex interplay
              between genes and their role in disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms.
